   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Andorra</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Principality in the southern Pyrenees
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Not to be confused with the Italian town of <a href="/wiki/Andora" title="Andora">Andora</a>.
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Andorra_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Andorra (disambiguation)">Andorra (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div> 
      <p class="mw-empty-elt"> </p>

      <p><b>Andorra</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɔːr/: 'ar' in 'war'">ɔːr</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span> <span class="nowrap" style="font-size:85%">(<span class="unicode haudio"><span class="fn"><span style="white-space:nowrap;margin-right:.25em;"><a href="/wiki/File:En-us-Andorra.ogg" title="About this sound"><img alt="About this sound" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/11px-Loudspeaker.svg.png" decoding="async" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/17px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Loudspeaker.svg/22px-Loudspeaker.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="20" data-file-height="20"></a></span><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/3e/En-us-Andorra.ogg" class="internal" title="En-us-Andorra.ogg">listen</a></span></span>)</span></span>, <span style="font-size:85%;">also</span> <span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><small><a href="/wiki/British_English" title="British English">UK</a>: </small><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/æ/: 'a' in 'bad'">æ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'d' in 'dye'">d</span><span title="/ɒr/: 'or' in 'moral'">ɒr</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>;<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <small>Catalan:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/Catalan" title="Help:IPA/Catalan">[ənˈdorə]</a></span>), officially the <b>Principality of Andorra</b> (<a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>: <i lang="ca">Principat d'Andorra</i>),<sup id="cite_ref-constitution_1-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-constitution-1">[1]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereignty" title="Sovereignty">sovereign</a> landlocked <a href="/wiki/Microstate" title="Microstate">microstate</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>, in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a>, bordered by <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> to the north and <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> to the south. Believed to have been created by <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a>, Andorra was ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Count of Urgell">count of Urgell</a> until 988, when it was transferred to the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_Urgell" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Urgell">Roman Catholic Diocese of Urgell</a>. The present principality was formed by <a href="/wiki/Par%C3%A9age_of_Andorra_1278" class="mw-redirect" title="Paréage of Andorra 1278">a charter in 1278</a>. It is known as a <a href="/wiki/Principality" title="Principality">principality</a> as it is a <a href="/wiki/Diarchy" title="Diarchy">diarchy</a> headed by two princes: the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Urgell">Bishop of Urgell</a> in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Catalonia, Spain">Catalonia, Spain</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_French_Republic" class="mw-redirect" title="President of the French Republic">President of the French Republic</a>. </p>
      <p>Andorra is the <a href="/wiki/European_microstates" title="European microstates">sixth-smallest nation in Europe</a>, having an area of 468 square kilometres (181&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) and a population of approximately 77,006.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-16">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Andorran_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Andorran people">Andorran people</a> are a <a href="/wiki/Italic_peoples" title="Italic peoples">Romance</a> ethnic group of originally <a href="/wiki/Catalans" title="Catalans">Catalan</a> descent.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-17">[17]</a></sup> Andorra is the 16th-smallest country in the world by land and the 11th-smallest by population.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> Its capital, <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a>, is the highest capital city in Europe, at an elevation of 1,023 metres (3,356 feet) <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> The official language is <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, but Spanish, Portuguese, and French are also commonly spoken.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Andorra" title="Tourism in Andorra">Tourism in Andorra</a> sees an estimated 10.2 million visitors annually.<sup id="cite_ref-es2_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-es2-21">[21]</a></sup> Andorra is not a member of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>, but the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> is its official currency. It has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> since 1993.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> In 2013, Andorra had <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_life_expectancy" title="List of countries by life expectancy">the highest life expectancy in the world</a> at 81 years, according to the <a href="/wiki/Global_Burden_of_Disease_Study" title="Global Burden of Disease Study">Global Burden of Disease Study</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The origin of the word Andorra is unknown, although several hypotheses have been formulated. The oldest derivation of the word Andorra is from the Greek historian <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">Polybius</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Histories_(Polybius)" title="The Histories (Polybius)">The Histories</a></i> III, 35, 1) who describes the Andosins, an <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberian</a> <a href="/wiki/Pre-Roman_peoples_of_the_Iberian_Peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-Roman peoples of the Iberian Peninsula">Pre-Roman tribe</a>, as historically located in the valleys of Andorra and facing the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">Carthaginian</a> army in its passage through the Pyrenees during the <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a>. The word Andosini or Andosins (Ἀνδοσίνοι) may derive from the <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> <i>handia</i> whose meaning is "big" or "giant".<sup id="cite_ref-Diccionari_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Diccionari-24">[24]</a></sup> The Andorran <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">toponymy</a> shows evidence of Basque language in the area. Another theory suggests that the word Andorra may derive from the old word Anorra that contains the Basque word <i>ur</i> (water).<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Another theory suggests that Andorra may derive from <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">الدارة</span>‎, <small><a href="/wiki/Romanization_of_Arabic" title="Romanization of Arabic">romanized</a>:&nbsp;</small><i lang="ar-Latn" title="Arabic-language romanization">al-darra</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[a]</a></sup> meaning "the thickly wooded place". When the <a href="/wiki/Arabs" title="Arabs">Arabs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a> conquered the Iberian Peninsula, the valleys of the High Pyrenees were covered by large tracts of forest. These regions were not administered by Muslims, because of the geographic difficulty of direct rule.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other theories suggest that the term derives from the <a href="/wiki/Navarro-Aragonese" title="Navarro-Aragonese">Navarro-Aragonese</a> andurrial, which means "land covered with bushes" or "scrubland".<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Folk_etymology" title="Folk etymology">folk etymology</a> holds that <a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> had named the region as a reference to the Biblical <a href="/wiki/Canaan" title="Canaan">Canaanite</a> valley of <a href="/wiki/Endor_(village)" title="Endor (village)">Endor</a> or <a href="/wiki/Endor_(village)" title="Endor (village)">Andor</a> (where the <a href="/wiki/Midianites" class="mw-redirect" title="Midianites">Midianites</a> had been defeated), a name bestowed by his heir and son <a href="/wiki/Louis_le_Debonnaire" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis le Debonnaire">Louis le Debonnaire</a> after defeating the Moors in the "wild valleys of Hell".<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">[29]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Andorra" title="History of Andorra">History of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prehistory">Prehistory</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Prehistory">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG/220px-Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG/330px-Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG/440px-Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gravats_del_Roc_de_les_Bruixes.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Roc de les Bruixes prehistorical sanctuary in <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">Canillo</a> (detail)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>La Balma de la <a href="/wiki/La_Margineda" title="La Margineda">Margineda</a>, found by archaeologists at <a href="/wiki/Sant_Juli%C3%A0_de_L%C3%B2ria" title="Sant Julià de Lòria">Sant Julià de Lòria</a>, was settled in 9,500 BC as a passing place between the two sides of the Pyrenees. The seasonal camp was perfectly located for hunting and fishing by the groups of hunter-gatherers from <a href="/wiki/Ari%C3%A8ge_(river)" title="Ariège (river)">Ariege</a> and <a href="/wiki/Segre_(river)" title="Segre (river)">Segre</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Age" class="mw-redirect" title="Neolithic Age">Neolithic Age</a>, a group of people moved to the <a href="/wiki/Madriu-Perafita-Claror_Valley" title="Madriu-Perafita-Claror Valley">Valley of Madriu</a> (the present-day Natural Parc located in <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a> declared <a href="/wiki/UNESCO_World_Heritage_Site" class="mw-redirect" title="UNESCO World Heritage Site">UNESCO World Heritage Site</a>) as a permanent camp in 6640 BC. The population of the valley grew cereals, raised domestic livestock, and developed a commercial trade with people from the <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A8gre_(department)" title="Sègre (department)">Segre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Occitania" title="Occitania">Occitania</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200932,_33_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200932,_33-32">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-33">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Other archaeological deposits include the Tombs of <a href="/wiki/Segudet" title="Segudet">Segudet</a> (<a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">Ordino</a>) and Feixa del Moro (Sant Julià de Lòria) both dated in 4900–4300 BC as an example of the <a href="/wiki/Urnfield_culture" title="Urnfield culture">Urn culture</a> in Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200932,_33_32-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200932,_33-32">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-33">[32]</a></sup> The model of small settlements began to evolve to a complex urbanism during the <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a>. <a href="/wiki/Metallurgy" title="Metallurgy">Metallurgical</a> items of iron, ancient coins, and relicaries can be found in the <a href="/wiki/Sanctuary" title="Sanctuary">ancient sanctuaries</a> scattered around the country. </p>
      <p>The sanctuary of Roc de les Bruixes (Stone of the Witches) is perhaps the most important archeological complex of this age in Andorra, located in the parish of <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">Canillo</a>, about the rituals of funerals, ancient scripture and engraved stone <a href="/wiki/Mural" title="Mural">murals</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200934,_35,_38,_39_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200934,_35,_38,_39-34">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_33-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-33">[32]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Iberian_and_Roman_Andorra">Iberian and Roman Andorra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Iberian and Roman Andorra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Ann%C3%ADbal,_andosins.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png/220px-Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png/330px-Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png/440px-Ann%C3%ADbal%2C_andosins.png 2x" data-file-width="819" data-file-height="834"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Ann%C3%ADbal,_andosins.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Hannibal" title="Hannibal">Hannibal</a>'s route (red) during the <a href="/wiki/Second_Punic_War" title="Second Punic War">Second Punic War</a>. The Iberian tribes (green) fought against the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Carthage" title="Ancient Carthage">Carthaginian</a> army in the Pyrenees.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The inhabitants of the valleys were traditionally associated with the <a href="/wiki/Iberians" title="Iberians">Iberians</a> and historically located in Andorra as the Iberian tribe Andosins or Andosini (Ἀνδοσίνους) during the 7th and 2nd centuries BC. Influenced by the <a href="/wiki/Aquitanian_language" title="Aquitanian language">Aquitanian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">Basque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Iberian_languages" title="Iberian languages">Iberian languages</a>, the locals developed some current toponyms. Early writings and documents relating to this group of people goes back to the second century BC by the Greek writer <a href="/wiki/Polybius" title="Polybius">Polybius</a> in his <i>Histories</i> during the <a href="/wiki/Punic_Wars" title="Punic Wars">Punic Wars</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200943_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200943-36">[35]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_33-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200936,_37_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200936,_37-37">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Some of the most significant remains of this era are the Castle of the Roc d'Enclar (part of the early <a href="/wiki/Marca_Hispanica" class="mw-redirect" title="Marca Hispanica">Marca Hispanica</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200944,_45,_46,_47_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200944,_45,_46,_47-38">[37]</a></sup> l'Anxiu in <a href="/wiki/Les_Escaldes" title="Les Escaldes">Les Escaldes</a> and Roc de L'Oral in <a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">Encamp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_33-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200936,_37_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200936,_37-37">[36]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The presence of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> influence is recorded from the 2nd century BC to the 5th century AD. The places found with more Roman presence are in Camp Vermell (Red Field) in Sant Julià de Lòria, and in some places in Encamp, as well as in the Roc d'Enclar. People continued trading, mainly with wine and cereals, with the Roman cities of <a href="/wiki/Urgellet" title="Urgellet">Urgellet</a> (the present-day <a href="/wiki/La_Seu_d%27Urgell" title="La Seu d'Urgell">La Seu d'Urgell</a>) and all across Segre through the <a href="/wiki/Roman_roads" title="Roman roads"><i>via romana</i></a> Strata Ceretana (also known as Strata Confluetana).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92_33-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200944_a_92-33">[32]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200952,_53_39-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200952,_53-39">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200944,_45,_46,_47_38-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200944,_45,_46,_47-38">[37]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visigoths_and_Carolingians:_the_legend_of_Charlemagne">Visigoths and Carolingians: the legend of Charlemagne</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Visigoths and Carolingians: the legend of Charlemagne">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/220px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="204" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/330px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/75/Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg/440px-Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg 2x" data-file-width="447" data-file-height="414"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Charlemagne_et_Louis_le_Pieux.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Charlemagne" title="Charlemagne">Charlemagne</a> instructing his son, <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">Louis the Pious</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_the_Roman_Empire" class="mw-redirect" title="Fall of the Roman Empire">fall of the Roman Empire</a>, Andorra came under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Visigothic_Kingdom" title="Visigothic Kingdom">Visigoths</a>, the <a href="/wiki/History_of_Toledo,_Spain#Visigothic_Toledo" title="History of Toledo, Spain">Kingdom of Toledo</a>, and from the <a href="/wiki/Diocese_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Diocese of Urgell">Diocese of Urgell</a>. The Visigoths remained in the valleys for 200 years, during which time <a href="/wiki/Gothic_Christianity" title="Gothic Christianity">Christianity</a> spread. When the <a href="/wiki/Al-Andalus" title="Al-Andalus">Muslim Empire of Al-Andalus</a> replaced the ruling Visigoths in most of the Iberian Peninsula, Andorra was sheltered from these invaders by the <a href="/wiki/Francia" title="Francia">Franks</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-40">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Tradition holds that Charles the Great (Charlemagne) granted a charter to the Andorran people for a contingent of five thousand soldiers under the command of Marc Almugaver, in return for fighting against the <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a> near <a href="/wiki/Port%C3%A9-Puymorens" title="Porté-Puymorens">Porté-Puymorens</a> (<a href="/wiki/Cerdanya" title="Cerdanya">Cerdanya</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[40]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png/220px-Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png/330px-Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png/440px-Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png 2x" data-file-width="591" data-file-height="400"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Parr%C3%B2quies_andorra.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The six old parishes named by their <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">patron saint</a> as depicted in the <i>Acta de Consagració i Dotació de la Catedral de la Seu d'Urgell</i> (839)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Andorra remained part of the <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_Marches" title="Hispanic Marches">Frankish <i>Marca Hispanica</i></a>, the buffer-zone between the <a href="/wiki/Francia" title="Francia">Frankish Empire</a> and the Muslim territories, Andorra being part of the territory ruled by the <a href="/wiki/Counts_of_Urgell" title="Counts of Urgell">Count of Urgell</a> and eventually by the <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Urgel" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Urgel">bishop</a> of the Diocese of Urgell. Also tradition holds that it was guaranteed by the son of Charlemagne, <a href="/wiki/Louis_the_Pious" title="Louis the Pious">Louis the Pious</a>, writing the <i>Carta de Poblament</i> or a local <a href="/wiki/Municipal_charter" title="Municipal charter">municipal charter</a> circa 805.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[41]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 988, <a href="/wiki/Borrell_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Borrell II">Borrell II</a>, Count of Urgell, gave the Andorran valleys to the Diocese of Urgell in exchange for land in Cerdanya.<sup id="cite_ref-histo1_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-histo1-43">[42]</a></sup> Since then, the Bishop of Urgell, based in Seu d'Urgell, has been <a href="/wiki/Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="Co-Princes of Andorra">Co-prince</a> of Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-elements_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elements-44">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first document that mentions Andorra as a territory is the <i>Acta de Consagració i Dotació de la Catedral de la Seu d'Urgell</i> (Deed of Consecration and Endowment of the Cathedral of La Seu d'Urgell). The old document dated from 839 depicts the six old <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Andorra" title="Parishes of Andorra">parishes</a> of the Andorran valleys and therefore the administrative division of the country.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-45">[44]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="Medieval_Age:_The_Par.C3.A9ages_and_the_founding_of_the_Co-Principality"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Medieval_Age:_The_Paréages_and_the_founding_of_the_Co-Principality">Medieval Age: The Paréages and the founding of the Co-Principality</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Medieval Age: The Paréages and the founding of the Co-Principality">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg/220px-Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg/330px-Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg/440px-Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2922" data-file-height="1864"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Joan_de_Caselles_-_7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Sant_Joan_de_Caselles" title="Sant Joan de Caselles">Sant Joan de Caselles</a> church, dating from the 11th century, part of the Andorran Romanesque heritage
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Before 1095, Andorra did not have any type of military protection and the Bishop of Urgell, who knew that the count of Urgell wanted to reclaim the Andorran valleys,<sup id="cite_ref-elements_44-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elements-44">[43]</a></sup> asked the <a href="/wiki/Lord_of_Caboet" title="Lord of Caboet">lord of Caboet</a> for help and protection. In 1095, the Lord of Caboet and the bishop of Urgell signed under oath a declaration of their co-sovereignty over Andorra. Arnalda, daughter of Arnau of Caboet, married the viscount of Castellbò. Their daughter, Ermessenda,<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> married the <a href="/wiki/Count_of_Foix" title="Count of Foix">count of Foix</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roger-Bernard_II,_Count_of_Foix" title="Roger-Bernard II, Count of Foix">Roger-Bernard II</a>. Roger-Bernard II and Ermessenda shared ruled over Andorra with the bishop of Urgell. </p>
      <p>In the 13th century, a military dispute arose between the bishop of Urgell and the count of Foix as aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Cathar_Crusade" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathar Crusade">Cathar Crusade</a>. The conflict was resolved in 1278 with the mediation of the <a href="/wiki/King_of_Aragon" class="mw-redirect" title="King of Aragon">king of Aragon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peter_III_of_Aragon" title="Peter III of Aragon">Peter III</a>, between the bishop and the count, by the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Par%C3%A9age_of_Andorra_1278" class="mw-redirect" title="Paréage of Andorra 1278">first paréage</a> which provided that Andorra's sovereignty be shared between the count of Foix<sup id="cite_ref-elements_44-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elements-44">[43]</a></sup> (whose title would ultimately transfer to the French head of state) and the bishop of Urgell, in <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>. This gave the principality its territory and political form.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-45">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009-47">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg/220px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg/330px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg/440px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1092" data-file-height="714"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall_-_14.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>1978 monument commemorating the 700th anniversary of the Paréages, located outside <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">Casa de la Vall</a> in the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg/220px-065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg/330px-065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg/440px-065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:065_Absis_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Apse fresco of <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters" title="Església de Sant Miquel d'Engolasters">Sant Miquel d'Engolasters</a> church, painted by Mestre de Santa Coloma during the 12th century<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>A second paréage was signed in 1288 after a dispute when the count of Foix ordered the construction of a castle in Roc d'Enclar.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_45-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-45">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009_47-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009-47">[46]</a></sup> The document was ratified by the noble notary <a href="/wiki/County_of_Cerdanya" title="County of Cerdanya">Jaume Orig of Puigcerdà</a> and the construction of military structures in the country was prohibited.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200960,_61_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200960,_61-49">[48]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146_45-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix200996_a_146-45">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1364 the political organization of the country named the figure of the <a href="/wiki/Syndic" title="Syndic">syndic</a> (now spokesman and president of the parliament) as representative of the Andorrans to their co-princes making possible the creation of <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Andorra" title="Parishes of Andorra">local departments</a> (comuns, quarts and veïnats). After being ratified by Bishop Francesc Tovia and Count <a href="/wiki/John_I,_Count_of_Foix" title="John I, Count of Foix">John I</a>, the Consell de la Terra or <a href="/wiki/General_Council_(Andorra)" title="General Council (Andorra)">Consell General de les Valls</a> (General Council of the Valleys) was founded in 1419, the second oldest parliament in Europe. The syndic Andreu d'Alàs and the General Council organized the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Andorra#Judicial_branch" title="Politics of Andorra">Justice Courts</a> (La Cort de Justicia) in 1433 with the co-Princes and the collection of taxes like foc i lloc (literally fire and site, a national tax active since then).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200978,_79,_80,_81,_88,_89_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200978,_79,_80,_81,_88,_89-50">[49]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_40-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-40">[39]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Although there are remains of ecclesiastical works dating before the 9th century (Sant Vicenç d'Enclar or <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Santa_Coloma" class="mw-redirect" title="Església de Santa Coloma">Església de Santa Coloma</a>), Andorra developed exquisite <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_Art_and_Architecture" class="mw-redirect" title="Romanesque Art and Architecture">Romanesque Art</a> during the 9th through 14th centuries, particularly in the construction of churches, bridges, religious murals and statues of the <a href="/wiki/Virgin_and_Child" class="mw-redirect" title="Virgin and Child">Virgin and Child</a> (<a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Meritxell" title="Our Lady of Meritxell">Our Lady of Meritxell</a> being the most important).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_40-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-40">[39]</a></sup> Nowadays, the <a href="/wiki/List_of_regional_characteristics_of_Romanesque_churches#Romanesque_churches_in_Spain,_Portugal_and_Andorra" title="List of regional characteristics of Romanesque churches">Romanesque</a> buildings that form part of <a href="/wiki/Cultural_Heritage_of_Andorra" title="Cultural Heritage of Andorra">Andorra's cultural heritage</a> stand out in a remarkable way, with an emphasis on <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Esteve" title="Església de Sant Esteve">Església de Sant Esteve</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sant_Joan_de_Caselles" title="Sant Joan de Caselles">Sant Joan de Caselles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esgl%C3%A9sia_de_Sant_Miquel_d%27Engolasters" title="Església de Sant Miquel d'Engolasters">Església de Sant Miquel d'Engolasters</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sant_Mart%C3%AD_de_la_Cortinada" class="mw-redirect" title="Sant Martí de la Cortinada">Sant Martí de la Cortinada</a> and the medieval bridges of <a href="/wiki/Pont_de_la_Margineda" title="Pont de la Margineda">Margineda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pont_dels_Escalls" title="Pont dels Escalls">Escalls</a> among many others.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200948,_49_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200948,_49-51">[50]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009150_a_194_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009150_a_194-52">[51]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Catalan Pyrenees were embryonic of the <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan language</a> at the end of the 11th century. Andorra was influenced by this language, which was adopted locally decades before it expanded to the rest of the Crown of Aragon.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The local population based its economy during the Middle Ages in livestock and agriculture, as well as in furs and weavers. Later, at the end of the 11th century, the first <a href="/wiki/Bloomery#Medieval_Europe" title="Bloomery">iron foundries</a> began to appear in Northern Parishes like <a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">Ordino</a>, much appreciated by the master artisans who developed the art of the forges, an important economic activity in the country from the 15th century.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009_40-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009-40">[39]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16th_to_18th_centuries">16th to 18th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 16th to 18th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG/220px-Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG/330px-Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fc/Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="266"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tribunal_de_Corts_d%27Andorra.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Main hall of <a href="/wiki/Andorra#Law_and_criminal_justice" title="Andorra">Tribunal de Corts</a> (High Court of Justice) inside <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">Casa de la Vall</a>, the central Judiciary Court of Andorra
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In 1601 the <a href="/wiki/Andorra#Law_and_criminal_justice" title="Andorra">Tribunal de Corts</a> (High Court of Justice) was created as a result of <a href="/wiki/Huguenot_rebellions" title="Huguenot rebellions">Huguenot rebellions</a> in France, <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Inquisition</a> courts coming from Spain and <a href="/wiki/Catalan_mythology_about_witches" title="Catalan mythology about witches">witchcraft-related beliefs native to the area</a>, in the context of the <a href="/wiki/Reformation" title="Reformation">Reformation</a> and <a href="/wiki/Counter-Reformation" title="Counter-Reformation">Counter-Reformation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50_54-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50-54">[53]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009108,_109_55-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009108,_109-55">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009238,_239_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009238,_239-56">[55]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>With the passage of time, the co-title to Andorra passed to the kings of <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Navarre" title="Kingdom of Navarre">Navarre</a>. After <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_France" title="Henry IV of France">Henry III of Navarre</a> became <a href="/wiki/King_of_France" class="mw-redirect" title="King of France">king of France</a>, he issued an edict in 1607 that established the head of the French state and the bishop of Urgell as <a href="/wiki/Co-Princes_of_Andorra" title="Co-Princes of Andorra">co-princes of Andorra</a>, a political arrangement that continues up to the present time. </p>
      <p>During 1617, communal councils form the sometent (popular militia or army) to deal with the rise of bandolerisme (<a href="/wiki/Brigandage" title="Brigandage">brigandage</a>) and the Consell de la Terra was defined and structured in terms of its composition, organization and competences current today.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50,_53,_54,_56_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199844,_45,_47,_48,_50,_53,_54,_56-57">[56]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Andorra continued with the same economic system that it had during the 12th–14th centuries with a large production of metallurgy (fargues, a system similar to Farga Catalana) and with the introduction of tobacco circa 1692 and import trade. The fair of Andorra la Vella was ratified by the co-princes in 1371 and 1448 being the most important annual national festival commercially ever since.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199814_58-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199814-58">[57]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199815_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199815-59">[58]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009134_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009134-60">[59]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg/220px-Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg/330px-Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/82/Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg/440px-Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5135" data-file-height="3423"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Building_in_Ordino._Andorra_216.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Manor_house" title="Manor house">Manor house</a> of the Rossell family in <a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">Ordino</a>, <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rossell" title="Casa Rossell">Casa Rossell</a>, built in 1611. The family also owned the largest ironwork forges in Andorra as Farga Rossell and Farga del Serrat.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The country had a unique and experienced <a href="/wiki/Guild" title="Guild">guild</a> of weavers, Confraria de Paraires i Teixidors, located in <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a> founded in 1604 taking advantage of the thermal waters of the area. By this time, the country was characterized by the social system of prohoms (wealthy society) and casalers (rest of the population with smaller economic acquisition), deriving from the tradition of <a href="/wiki/Pubilla" title="Pubilla">pubilla</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heir" class="mw-redirect" title="Heir">hereu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199820,_21_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199820,_21-62">[61]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009106,_107_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009106,_107-63">[62]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009105,_106,_107,_140,_141_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009105,_106,_107,_140,_141-64">[63]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009263_a_270_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009263_a_270-65">[64]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Three centuries after its foundation the Consell de la Terra located its headquarters and the Tribunal de Corts in <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">Casa de la Vall</a> in 1702. The <a href="/wiki/Manor_house" title="Manor house">manor house</a> built in 1580 served as a noble fortress of the Busquets family. Inside the parliament was placed the Closet of the six keys (Armari de les sis claus) representative of each Andorran parish and where the <a href="/wiki/Andorran_constitution" class="mw-redirect" title="Andorran constitution">Andorran constitution</a> and other documents and laws were kept later on.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199860_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199860-66">[65]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200982_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton200982-67">[66]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In both the <a href="/wiki/Reapers%27_War" title="Reapers' War">Reapers' War</a> and the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Spanish_Succession" title="War of the Spanish Succession">War of the Spanish Succession</a>, the Andorran people (although professing to be a neutral country) supported the <a href="/wiki/Catalans" title="Catalans">Catalans</a> who saw their <a href="/wiki/Catalan_constitutions" title="Catalan constitutions">rights</a> reduced in <a href="/wiki/Nueva_Planta_decrees" title="Nueva Planta decrees">1716</a>. The reaction was the promotion of Catalan writings in Andorra, with cultural works such as the <i>Book of Privileges</i> (<i>Llibre de Privilegis de 1674</i>), <i>Manual Digest</i> (1748) by Antoni Fiter i Rossell or the <i>Polità andorrà</i> (1763) by Antoni Puig.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009229-68">[67]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199849_a_52,_i_57,_58_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTELlop_Rovira199849_a_52,_i_57,_58-69">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><span class="anchor" id="New_Reform_of_Andorra"></span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century:_the_New_Reform_and_the_Andorran_Question">19th century: the New Reform and the Andorran Question</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 19th century: the New Reform and the Andorran Question">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit_(cropped).png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit_%28cropped%29.png/170px-Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit_%28cropped%29.png" decoding="async" width="170" height="205" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit_%28cropped%29.png/255px-Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit_%28cropped%29.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit_%28cropped%29.png/340px-Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit_%28cropped%29.png 2x" data-file-width="341" data-file-height="412"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit_(cropped).png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit" title="Guillem d'Areny-Plandolit">Guillem d'Areny-Plandolit</a> led the New Reform of 1866.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>After the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/Napoleon_I" class="mw-redirect" title="Napoleon I">Napoleon I</a> reestablished the Co-Principate in 1809 and removed the French medieval title. In 1812–1813, the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a> annexed Catalonia during the <a href="/wiki/Peninsular_War" title="Peninsular War">Peninsular War</a> (<i lang="ca" title="Catalan-language text">Guerra Peninsular</i>) and divided the region into four <a href="/wiki/D%C3%A9partement" class="mw-redirect" title="Département">départements</a>, with Andorra as a part of the district of <a href="/wiki/Puigcerd%C3%A0" title="Puigcerdà">Puigcerdà</a>. In 1814, an imperial decree reestablished the independence and economy of Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009172_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009172-70">[69]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009172_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009172-71">[70]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009342–343_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009342–343-72">[71]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>During this period, Andorra's late medieval institutions and rural culture remained largely unchanged. In 1866, the <a href="/wiki/Syndic" title="Syndic">syndic</a> <a href="/wiki/Guillem_d%27Areny-Plandolit" title="Guillem d'Areny-Plandolit">Guillem d'Areny-Plandolit</a> led the reformist group in a Council General of 24 members elected by suffrage limited to heads of families. The Council General replaced the aristocratic oligarchy that previously ruled the state.<sup id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-73">[72]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The New Reform (<i lang="ca" title="Catalan-language text">Nova Reforma</i>) began after ratification by both Co-Princes and established the basis of the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Andorra" title="Constitution of Andorra">constitution</a><sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[73]</a></sup> and symbols—such as the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Andorra" title="Flag of Andorra">tricolor flag</a>—of Andorra. A new <a href="/wiki/Service_economy" title="Service economy">service economy</a> arose as a demand of the valley inhabitants and began to build infrastructure such as hotels, spa resorts, roads and telegraph lines.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009192–193_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009192–193-75">[74]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009191–193_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009191–193-76">[75]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009345–347_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009345–347-77">[76]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:192px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg/190px-Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg" decoding="async" width="190" height="288" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/4/47/Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="263" data-file-height="398"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Revoluci%C3%B3_de_1881_d%27Andorra.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">Canillo</a> scenery during the Revolution of 1881<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The authorities of the Co-Princes banned casinos and betting houses throughout the country. The ban resulted in an economic conflict for the Andorran people. The conflict led to the so-called revolution of 1881, when revolutionaries assaulted the house of the syndic on 8 December 1880, and established the Provisional Revolutionary Council led by Joan Pla i Calvo and Pere Baró i Mas. The Provisional Revolutionary Council allowed for the construction of casinos and spas by foreign companies.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009198–203_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009198–203-79">[78]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>From 7 to 9 June 1881, the loyalists of <a href="/wiki/Canillo" title="Canillo">Canillo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">Encamp</a> reconquered the parishes of <a href="/wiki/Ordino" title="Ordino">Ordino</a> and <a href="/wiki/La_Massana" title="La Massana">La Massana</a> by establishing contact with the revolutionary forces in <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199859–63_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199859–63-80">[79]</a></sup> After a day of combat the <a href="/wiki/Pont_dels_Escalls" title="Pont dels Escalls">Treaty of the Bridge of Escalls</a> was signed on 10 June.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199658–65_81-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199658–65-81">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009194–195_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009194–195-82">[81]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009348–350_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009348–350-83">[82]</a></sup> The council was replaced and new elections were held. The economic situation worsened, as the populace was divided over the <i lang="ca" title="Catalan-language text">Qüestió d'Andorra</i>&nbsp;– the "Andorran Question" in relation to the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Question" title="Eastern Question">Eastern Question</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199864–68_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199864–68-84">[83]</a></sup> The struggles continued between pro-bishops, pro-French, and nationalists based on the troubles of Canillo in 1882 and 1885.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199667–70_85-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199667–70-85">[84]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009198–203_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEGuillamet_Anton2009198–203-86">[85]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009352–353_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009352–353-87">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Andorra participated in the cultural movement of the Catalan <a href="/wiki/Renaixen%C3%A7a" title="Renaixença">Renaixença</a>. Between 1882 and 1887, the first academic schools were formed where trilingualism coexisted with the official language, Catalan. <a href="/wiki/Romanticism" title="Romanticism">Romantic</a> authors from France and Spain reported the awakening of the <a href="/wiki/Romantic_nationalism" title="Romantic nationalism">national consciousness</a> of the country. <a href="/wiki/Jacint_Verdaguer" title="Jacint Verdaguer">Jacint Verdaguer</a> lived in Ordino during the 1880s where he wrote and shared works related to the Renaixença with writer and photographer, <a href="/wiki/Casa_Rossell" title="Casa Rossell">Joaquim de Riba</a>. </p>
      <p>In 1848, <a href="/wiki/Fromental_Hal%C3%A9vy" title="Fromental Halévy">Fromental Halévy</a> had premiered the opera <i><a href="/wiki/Le_val_d%27Andorre" title="Le val d'Andorre">Le Val d'Andorre</a></i> to great success in Europe, where the national consciousness of the valleys was exposed in the romantic work during the Peninsular War.<sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199878–81_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEPeruga_Guerrero199878–81-88">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199674_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEMinisteri_d'Educació,_Joventut_i_Esports199674-89">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009354–357_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FOOTNOTEArmengol_Aleix2009354–357-90">[89]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_and_21st_century:_Modernisation_of_the_country_and_the_Constitutional_Andorra">20th and 21st century: Modernisation of the country and the Constitutional Andorra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 20th and 21st century: Modernisation of the country and the Constitutional Andorra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Skossyreff_Writing_Constitution.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Skossyreff_Writing_Constitution.png/180px-Skossyreff_Writing_Constitution.png" decoding="async" width="180" height="112" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Skossyreff_Writing_Constitution.png/270px-Skossyreff_Writing_Constitution.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Skossyreff_Writing_Constitution.png/360px-Skossyreff_Writing_Constitution.png 2x" data-file-width="2014" data-file-height="1254"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Skossyreff_Writing_Constitution.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Boris_Skossyreff" title="Boris Skossyreff">Boris Skossyreff</a>, briefly self-proclaimed King of Andorra in 1934
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Andorra declared war on <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Germany" class="mw-redirect" title="Imperial Germany">Imperial Germany</a> during World War I, but did not take part directly in the fighting. Some Andorrans volunteered to take part in the conflict as part of the <a href="/wiki/Marching_Regiment_of_the_Foreign_Legion" title="Marching Regiment of the Foreign Legion">French Legions</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup> It remained in an official state of <a href="/wiki/Belligerency" class="mw-redirect" title="Belligerency">belligerency</a> until 1958 as it was not included in the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DYKAndorra_92-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DYKAndorra-92">[91]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1933, France occupied Andorra following social unrest which occurred before elections due to the <a href="/wiki/Andorran_Revolution" title="Andorran Revolution">Revolution of 1933</a> and the FHASA strikes (Vagues de FHASA); the revolt led by <a href="/wiki/Young_Andorrans" class="mw-redirect" title="Young Andorrans">Joves Andorrans</a> (a <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">labour union group</a> related to the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Confederaci%C3%B3n_Nacional_del_Trabajo" title="Confederación Nacional del Trabajo">CNT</a> and <a href="/wiki/Federaci%C3%B3n_Anarquista_Ib%C3%A9rica" title="Federación Anarquista Ibérica">FAI</a>) called for political reforms,<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Universal_suffrage" title="Universal suffrage">universal suffrage vote</a> of all Andorrans and acted in defense of the rights of local and foreign workers during the construction of FHASA's hydroelectric power station in <a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">Encamp</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[93]</a></sup> On 5 April 1933 Joves Andorrans seized the Andorran Parliament.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup> These actions were preceded by the arrival of Colonel René-Jules Baulard with 50 <a href="/wiki/National_Gendarmerie" title="National Gendarmerie">gendarmes</a> and the mobilization of 200 local militias or sometent led by the Síndic Francesc Cairat.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[95]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 6 July 1934, adventurer and nobleman <a href="/wiki/Boris_Skossyreff" title="Boris Skossyreff">Boris Skossyreff</a>, with his promise of freedoms and modernization of the country and wealth through the establishment of a tax haven and foreign investments, received the support of the members of the General Council to proclaim himself the sovereign of Andorra. On 8 July 1934 Boris issued a proclamation in Urgell, declaring himself Boris I, King of Andorra,<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[96]</a></sup> simultaneously declaring war on the Bishop of Urgell and approving the King's constitution on 10 July.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> He was arrested by the Co-Prince and Bishop <a href="/wiki/Just%C3%AD_Guitart_i_Vilardeb%C3%B3" title="Justí Guitart i Vilardebó">Justí Guitart i Vilardebó</a> and their authorities on 20 July and ultimately expelled from Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup> From 1936 until 1940, a French military detachment of <a href="/wiki/Garde_Mobile" title="Garde Mobile">Garde Mobile</a> led by well-known Colonel René-Jules Baulard was garrisoned in Andorra to secure the principality against disruption from the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a><sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Francoist_Spain" title="Francoist Spain">Francoist Spain</a><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[100]</a></sup> and also face the rise of <a href="/wiki/Republicanism" title="Republicanism">Republicanism</a> in the aftermath of the 1933 Revolution.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> During the Spanish Civil War, the inhabitants of Andorra welcomed refugees from both sides, and many of them settled permanently in the country thus contributing to the subsequent economic boom and the entry into the <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">capitalist era</a> of Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-qucut.com_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qucut.com-104">[103]</a></sup> Francoist troops reached the Andorran border in the later stages of the war.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:22B_andorra_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/22B_andorra_2.jpg/220px-22B_andorra_2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/22B_andorra_2.jpg/330px-22B_andorra_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/22B_andorra_2.jpg/440px-22B_andorra_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="785" data-file-height="388"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:22B_andorra_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Enthronement as Co-Prince in 1942 of Bishop <a href="/wiki/Ramon_Iglesias_i_Navarri" class="mw-redirect" title="Ramon Iglesias i Navarri">Ramón Iglesias</a> (center). The local comite was led by Francesc Cairat (left), the <a href="/wiki/List_of_First_Syndics_of_the_General_Council" title="List of First Syndics of the General Council">First General Syndic</a> with the longest regencie, from 1936 to 1960.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>During World War II, Andorra remained neutral and was an important smuggling route between <a href="/wiki/Vichy_France" title="Vichy France">Vichy France</a> and Francoist Spain,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup> two fascist states. Many Andorrans criticized the passivity of the General Council for impeding both the entry and expulsion of foreigners and refugees, committing economic crimes,<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup> reducing the rights of citizens<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup> and being sympathetic to <a href="/wiki/Francoism" class="mw-redirect" title="Francoism">Francoism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-iec.cat_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iec.cat-111">[110]</a></sup> General Council members justified the council's political and diplomatic actions as necessary for Andorra's survival and the protection of its sovereignty. Andorra was relatively unscathed by the two world wars and the Spanish Civil War.<sup id="cite_ref-iec.cat_111-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iec.cat-111">[110]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[111]</a></sup> Certain <a href="/wiki/Resistance_during_World_War_II" title="Resistance during World War II">groups</a> organized themselves to help victims of oppression in Nazi-occupied countries, while participating in smuggling to help Andorra survive. Among the groups that were most prominent there was the <a href="/wiki/Hostal_Palanques" title="Hostal Palanques">Hostal Palanques</a> Evasion Network Command. The Evasion Network Command, in contact with the British <a href="/wiki/Mi6" class="mw-redirect" title="Mi6">Mi6</a>, helped almost 400 fugitives,<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup> among whom were <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Allied</a> military personnel.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> The Command remained active between 1941 and 1944, although there were struggles with <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">pro-Axis</a> informers and <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">Gestapo</a> agents within Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:23-24.10.67._De_Gaulle_en_Andorre_(1967)_-_53Fi5569.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/23-24.10.67._De_Gaulle_en_Andorre_%281967%29_-_53Fi5569.jpg/220px-23-24.10.67._De_Gaulle_en_Andorre_%281967%29_-_53Fi5569.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/23-24.10.67._De_Gaulle_en_Andorre_%281967%29_-_53Fi5569.jpg/330px-23-24.10.67._De_Gaulle_en_Andorre_%281967%29_-_53Fi5569.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/23-24.10.67._De_Gaulle_en_Andorre_%281967%29_-_53Fi5569.jpg/440px-23-24.10.67._De_Gaulle_en_Andorre_%281967%29_-_53Fi5569.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1816" data-file-height="1820"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:23-24.10.67._De_Gaulle_en_Andorre_(1967)_-_53Fi5569.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Co-Prince <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> in the streets of Sant Julià de Lòria in Andorra, October 1967
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In the capital city there was a smuggling <a href="/wiki/Black_market" title="Black market">black market</a> network of propaganda, culture and cinematic art not prone to totalitarian regimes, promulgated in some places as the Hotel Mirador or the Casino Hotel,<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[116]</a></sup> as a meeting place for people of ideologies close to Andorran and <a href="/wiki/Spanish_republicanism" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish republicanism">Spanish Republicanism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Free_France" title="Free France">Free France</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The network was maintained after the war, when film societies were formed, where movies, music and books <a href="/wiki/Censorship_in_Francoist_Spain" title="Censorship in Francoist Spain">censored in Franco's Spain</a> were imported, thus becoming an anti-censorship attraction for the Catalan or foreign public even within Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-qucut.com_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qucut.com-104">[103]</a></sup> Andorran Group (Agrupament Andorrà), an <a href="/wiki/Anti-fascism" title="Anti-fascism">anti-fascist organization</a> linked to the Occitanie's <a href="/wiki/French_Resistance" title="French Resistance">French Resistance</a>, accused the French representative (veguer) of <a href="/wiki/Collaboration_with_the_Axis_Powers" title="Collaboration with the Axis Powers">collaboration with Nazism</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[117]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The Andorran opening to the <a href="/wiki/Capitalist_economy" class="mw-redirect" title="Capitalist economy">capitalist economy</a> resulted in two axes: mass tourism and the country's tax exemption. The first steps toward the capitalist boom date from the 1930s, with the construction of FHASA<sup id="cite_ref-iec.cat1_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iec.cat1-119">[118]</a></sup> and the creation of professional banking<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup> with <a href="/wiki/Andbank" title="Andbank">Banc Agrícol</a> (1930) and <a href="/wiki/Cr%C3%A8dit_Andorr%C3%A0" title="Crèdit Andorrà">Crèdit Andorrà</a> (1949), later with <a href="/wiki/Mora_Banc_Grup" title="Mora Banc Grup">Banca Mora</a> (1952), <a href="/wiki/Banca_Privada_d%27Andorra" title="Banca Privada d'Andorra">Banca Cassany</a> (1958) and <a href="/w/index.php?title=SOBANCA&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="SOBANCA (page does not exist)">SOBANCA</a> (1960). Shortly after activities such as skiing and shopping become a tourist attraction, with the inauguration of ski resorts and cultural entities in the late 1930s.<sup id="cite_ref-iec.cat1_119-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iec.cat1-119">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup> All in all, a renovated hotel industry has developed. In April 1968 a social health insurance system was created (<a href="/wiki/Caixa_Andorrana_de_Seguretat_Social" title="Caixa Andorrana de Seguretat Social">CASS</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[121]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Andorra_-_panoramio_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Andorra_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg/220px-Andorra_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Andorra_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg/330px-Andorra_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/Andorra_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg/440px-Andorra_-_panoramio_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Andorra_-_panoramio_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Streets of the city centre of Andorra la Vella in 1986. From the same year until 1989 Andorra normalized the economic treaties with the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">EEC</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Gilbert_Saboya_Sebastian_Kurz_(13927283877).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Gilbert_Saboya_Sebastian_Kurz_%2813927283877%29.jpg/220px-Gilbert_Saboya_Sebastian_Kurz_%2813927283877%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Gilbert_Saboya_Sebastian_Kurz_%2813927283877%29.jpg/330px-Gilbert_Saboya_Sebastian_Kurz_%2813927283877%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/77/Gilbert_Saboya_Sebastian_Kurz_%2813927283877%29.jpg/440px-Gilbert_Saboya_Sebastian_Kurz_%2813927283877%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3070" data-file-height="2126"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Gilbert_Saboya_Sebastian_Kurz_(13927283877).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Foreign Minister of Andorra <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_Saboya_Sunye" class="mw-redirect" title="Gilbert Saboya Sunye">Gilbert Saboya</a> meeting Austrian foreign minister <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_Kurz" title="Sebastian Kurz">Sebastian Kurz</a> at the <a href="/wiki/Committee_of_Ministers_of_the_Council_of_Europe" title="Committee of Ministers of the Council of Europe">Committee of Ministers of the Council of Europe</a> in 2014
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Andorran Government necessarily involved planning, projection and forecasts for the future: with the official visit of the French co-prince <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> in 1967 and 1969, it was given approval for the economic boom and national demands within the framework of human rights and international openness.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Andorra lived an era commonly known as "Andorran dream"<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> (in relation to the <a href="/wiki/American_Dream" title="American Dream">American dream</a>) along with the <a href="/wiki/Trente_Glorieuses" title="Trente Glorieuses">Trente Glorieuses</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Mass_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Mass culture">mass culture</a> rooted the country experiencing radical changes in the economy and culture. Proof of this event was <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A0dio_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="Ràdio Andorra">Ràdio Andorra</a>, number one transmitter musical radio station in Europe in this period,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> with guests and speakers of great importance promoting musical hits of <a href="/wiki/Chanson_fran%C3%A7aise" class="mw-redirect" title="Chanson française">chanson française</a>, <a href="/wiki/Swing_(dance)" title="Swing (dance)">swing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_%26_blues" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhythm &amp; blues">rhythm &amp; blues</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">jazz</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_and_roll" title="Rock and roll">rock and roll</a> or <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">American country music</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> During this period Andorra achieved a <a href="/wiki/GDP" class="mw-redirect" title="GDP">GDP</a> per capita and a life expectancy higher than the most standard countries of the current economy.<sup id="cite_ref-iec.cat1_119-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-iec.cat1-119">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[129]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Given its relative isolation, Andorra has existed outside the mainstream of European history, with few ties to countries other than France, Spain and Portugal. In recent times, however, its thriving tourist industry along with developments in transport and communications have removed the country from its isolation. Since 1976 the country sees the need to reform Andorran institutions due to the anachronisms in the field of sovereignty, human rights and the balance of powers as well as the need to adapt legislation to modern demands.
