In 1982 a first separation of powers took place when instituting the Govern d'Andorra, under the name of Executive Board (Consell Executiu), chaired by the first prime minister <a href="/wiki/%C3%92scar_Ribas_Reig" title="Òscar Ribas Reig">Òscar Ribas Reig</a> with the approval of the Co-Princes.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> In 1989 the Principality signed an agreement with the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> to regularize trade relations.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Its political system was modernized in 1993 after the <a href="/wiki/Andorran_constitutional_referendum,_1993" class="mw-redirect" title="Andorran constitutional referendum, 1993">Andorran constitutional referendum</a>, when the <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Andorra" title="Constitution of Andorra">constitution</a> was drafted by the Co-Princes and the General Council and approved on 14 March<sup id="cite_ref-NS_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NS-133">[132]</a></sup> by 74.2% of voters, with a 76% turnout.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Andorran_parliamentary_election,_1993" class="mw-redirect" title="Andorran parliamentary election, 1993">first elections</a> under the new constitution were held later in the year.<sup id="cite_ref-NS_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NS-133">[132]</a></sup> The same year Andorra became a member of the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Andorra formalized diplomatic relations with the United States in 1996 participating in the 51st <a href="/wiki/UN_General_Assembly" class="mw-redirect" title="UN General Assembly">UN General Assembly</a>, a very important fact in view of the normalization that the country aspired to. First General Syndic <a href="/wiki/Marc_Forn%C3%A9_Moln%C3%A9" title="Marc Forné Molné">Marc Forné</a> took part on a speech in Catalan in the General Assembly to defend the reform of the organization, and after three days Forné took part in the parliamentary assembly of the Council of Europe to defend the linguistic rights and the economy of Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> In mid-2006 the monetary agreement with the European Union is formalized, which allows Andorra to use the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> in an official way, as well as coin its own Euro currency.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Politics">Politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Andorra" title="Politics of Andorra">Politics of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Co-princes_of_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-princes of Andorra">Co-princes of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{display:flex;flex-direction:column}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{display:flex;flex-direction:row;clear:left;flex-wrap:wrap;width:100%;box-sizing:border-box}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{margin:1px;float:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .theader{clear:both;font-weight:bold;text-align:center;align-self:center;background-color:transparent;width:100%}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbcaption{background-color:transparent}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-left{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-right{text-align:right}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .text-align-center{text-align:center}@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti .thumbinner{width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;max-width:none!important;align-items:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow{justify-content:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style>
      <div class="thumb tmulti tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:290px;max-width:290px">
        <div class="trow">
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:152px;max-width:152px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Mons._Vives_(30612833490).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg/150px-Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="150" height="189" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg/225px-Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/30/Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg/300px-Mons._Vives_%2830612833490%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="755"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <b><a href="/wiki/Joan_Enric_Vives_i_Sic%C3%ADlia" title="Joan Enric Vives i Sicília">Joan Enric Vives i Sicília</a></b>
           <br>&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Urgell">Bishop of Urgell</a> since 12 May 2003
          </div>
         </div>
         <div class="tsingle" style="width:134px;max-width:134px">
          <div class="thumbimage">
           <a href="/wiki/File:Emmanuel_Macron_(cropped).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Emmanuel_Macron_%28cropped%29.jpg/132px-Emmanuel_Macron_%28cropped%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="132" height="189" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Emmanuel_Macron_%28cropped%29.jpg/198px-Emmanuel_Macron_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c3/Emmanuel_Macron_%28cropped%29.jpg/264px-Emmanuel_Macron_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="441" data-file-height="630"></a>
          </div>
          <div class="thumbcaption">
           <b><a href="/wiki/Emmanuel_Macron" title="Emmanuel Macron">Emmanuel Macron</a></b>
           <br>&nbsp;– <a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">President of France</a> since 14 May 2017
          </div>
         </div>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Andorra is a parliamentary <a href="/wiki/Co-principality" class="mw-redirect" title="Co-principality">co-principality</a> with the president of France and the Catholic <a href="/wiki/Bishop_of_Urgell" class="mw-redirect" title="Bishop of Urgell">bishop of Urgell</a> (<a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, Spain) as <a href="/wiki/List_of_Co-Princes_of_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Co-Princes of Andorra">co-princes</a>. This peculiarity makes the president of France, in his capacity as <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="Prince of Andorra">prince of Andorra</a>, an elected monarch, although he is not elected by a popular vote of the Andorran people. The politics of Andorra take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary</a> <a href="/wiki/Representative_democracy" title="Representative democracy">representative democracy</a>, whereby the <a href="/wiki/List_of_heads_of_government_of_Andorra" title="List of heads of government of Andorra">head of government</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">chief executive</a>, and of a <a href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/pluriform" class="extiw" title="wikt:pluriform">pluriform</a> multi-party system. </p>
      <p>The current head of government is <a href="/wiki/Xavier_Espot_Zamora" class="mw-redirect" title="Xavier Espot Zamora">Xavier Espot Zamora</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Democrats_for_Andorra" title="Democrats for Andorra">Democrats for Andorra</a> (DA). <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" class="mw-redirect" title="Executive power">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. Legislative power is vested in both government and parliament. </p>
      <p>The Parliament of Andorra is known as the General Council. The General Council consists of between 28 and 42 councillors. The councillors serve for four-year terms, and elections are held between the 30th and 40th days following the dissolution of the previous Council. </p>
      <p>Half are elected in equal numbers by each of the seven administrative parishes, and the other half of the councillors are elected in a single national constituency. Fifteen days after the election, the councillors hold their inauguration. During this session, the Syndic General, who is the head of the General Council, and the Subsyndic General, his assistant, are elected. Eight days later, the Council convenes once more. During this session the head of government is chosen from among the councillors. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg/220px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="137" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg/330px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg/440px-Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3560" data-file-height="2222"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall_-_18.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Casa de la Vall, the historical and ceremonial Andorran Parliament
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Candidates can be proposed by a minimum of one-fifth of the councillors. The Council then elects the candidate with the absolute majority of votes to be head of government. The Syndic General then notifies the co-princes, who in turn appoint the elected candidate as the head of government of Andorra. The General Council is also responsible for proposing and passing laws. Bills may be presented to the council as Private Members' Bills by three of the local Parish Councils jointly or by at least one tenth of the citizens of Andorra. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall,_Andorra_la_Vieja,_Andorra,_2013-12-30,_DD_03.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG/220px-Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="78" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG/330px-Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG/440px-Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Andorra_la_Vieja%2C_Andorra%2C_2013-12-30%2C_DD_03.JPG 2x" data-file-width="5426" data-file-height="1933"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Casa_de_la_Vall,_Andorra_la_Vieja,_Andorra,_2013-12-30,_DD_03.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The <a href="/wiki/New_Parliament_of_Andorra" title="New Parliament of Andorra">New Parliament of Andorra</a>, headquarters of the <a href="/wiki/General_Council_of_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="General Council of Andorra">General Council</a> since 2011, next to <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_la_Vall" title="Casa de la Vall">Casa de la Vall</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The council also approves the annual budget of the principality. The government must submit the proposed budget for parliamentary approval at least two months before the previous budget expires. If the budget is not approved by the first day of the next year, the previous budget is extended until a new one is approved. Once any bill is approved, the Syndic General is responsible for presenting it to the Co-Princes so that they may sign and enact it. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Els_7_poetes,_Casa_de_la_Vall,_Consell_General.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG/220px-Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG/330px-Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG/440px-Els_7_poetes%2C_Casa_de_la_Vall%2C_Consell_General.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Els_7_poetes,_Casa_de_la_Vall,_Consell_General.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The centre of government in <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>If the head of government is not satisfied with the council, he may request that the co-princes dissolve the council and order new elections. In turn, the councillors have the power to remove the head of government from office. After a motion of censure is approved by at least one-fifth of the councillors, the council will vote and if it receives the absolute majority of votes, the head of government is removed. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Law_and_criminal_justice">Law and criminal justice</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Law and criminal justice">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Law_of_Andorra" title="Law of Andorra">Law of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The judiciary is composed of the Magistrates Court, the Criminal Law Court, the High Court of Andorra, and the Constitutional Court. The High Court of Justice is composed of five judges: one appointed by the head of government, one each by the co-princes, one by the Syndic General, and one by the judges and magistrates. It is presided over by the member appointed by the Syndic General and the judges hold office for six-year terms. </p>
      <p>The magistrates and judges are appointed by the High Court, as is the president of the Criminal Law Court. The High Court also appoints members of the Office of the Attorney General. The Constitutional Court is responsible for interpreting the Constitution and reviewing all appeals of unconstitutionality against laws and treaties. It is composed of four judges, one appointed by each of the co-princes and two by the General Council. They serve eight-year terms. The Court is presided over by one of the judges on a two-year rotation so that each judge at one point will preside over the Court. </p> 
      <h2><span id="Foreign_relations.2C_defence.2C_and_security"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations,_defence,_and_security">Foreign relations, defence, and security</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Foreign relations, defence, and security">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_Andorra" title="Foreign relations of Andorra">Foreign relations of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg/220px-Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg/330px-Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg/440px-Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="3888"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Bruxelles_rue_de_la_Montagne_10.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The embassy of Andorra in <a href="/wiki/Brussels" title="Brussels">Brussels</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Andorra does not have its own armed forces,<sup id="cite_ref-cia_3-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> although there is a small ceremonial army. Responsibility for defending the nation rests primarily with France and Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> However, in case of emergencies or natural disasters, the Sometent (an alarm) is called and all able-bodied men between 21 and 60 of Andorran nationality must serve.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-recarrega.net_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recarrega.net-141">[140]</a></sup> This is why all Andorrans, and especially the head of each house (usually the eldest able-bodied man of a house) should, by law, keep a rifle, even though the law also states that the police will offer a firearm in case of need.<sup id="cite_ref-recarrega.net_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-recarrega.net-141">[140]</a></sup> Andorra is a full member of the United Nations (UN), the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_Security_and_Co-operation_in_Europe" title="Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe">Organization for Security and Co-operation in Europe</a> (OSCE), and has a special agreement with the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (EU), it also has observer status at the <a href="/wiki/World_Trade_Organization" title="World Trade Organization">World Trade Organization</a> (WTO).<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup> On 16 October 2020, Andorra became the 190th member of the <a href="/wiki/International_Monetary_Fund" title="International Monetary Fund">International Monetary Fund</a> (IMF), during the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Military">Military</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Military">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Andorra has a small army, which has historically been raised or reconstituted at various dates, but has never in modern times amounted to a standing army. The basic principle of Andorran defence is that all able-bodied men are available to fight if called upon by the sounding of the Sometent. Being a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a>, Andorra has no navy. </p>
      <p>Before World War I, Andorra maintained an armed force of about 600 part-time militiamen under the supervision of a Captain (Capità or Cap de Sometent) and a Lieutenant (Desener or Lloctinent del Capità). This body was not liable for service outside the principality and was commanded by two officials (veguers) appointed by France and the Bishop of Urgell.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[144]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Despite not being involved in any fighting during the First World War, Andorra was technically the longest combatant, as the country was left out of the <a href="/wiki/Versailles_Peace_Conference" class="mw-redirect" title="Versailles Peace Conference">Versailles Peace Conference</a>, <a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">technically</a> remaining at war with Germany from its original declaration of war in 1914 until 24 September 1958 when Andorra officially declared peace with Germany.<sup id="cite_ref-DYKAndorra_92-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DYKAndorra-92">[91]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[145]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In the modern era, the army has consisted of a very small body of volunteers willing to undertake ceremonial duties. Uniforms and weaponry were handed down from generation to generation within families and communities.<sup id="cite_ref-elperiodic.ad_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elperiodic.ad-147">[146]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The army's role in internal security was largely taken over by the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Police_Corps_of_Andorra" title="Police Corps of Andorra">Police Corps of Andorra</a> in 1931. Brief civil disorder associated with the elections of 1933 led to assistance being sought from the French <a href="/wiki/National_Gendarmerie" title="National Gendarmerie">National Gendarmerie</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[147]</a></sup> with a detachment resident in Andorra for two months under the command of René-Jules Baulard.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The Andorran Police was reformed in the following year, with eleven soldiers appointed to supervisory roles.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[148]</a></sup> The force consisted of six <a href="/wiki/Corporal" title="Corporal">Corporals</a>, one for each parish (although there are currently seven parishes, there were only six until 1978), plus four junior staff officers to co-ordinate action, and a commander with the rank of major. It was the responsibility of the six corporals, each in his own parish, to be able to raise a fighting force from among the able-bodied men of the parish. </p>
      <p>Today a small, twelve-man ceremonial unit remains the only permanent section of the Sometent, but all able-bodied men remain technically available for military service,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[149]</a></sup> with a requirement for each family to have access to a firearm. A shotgun per household is unregulated. Rifles and pistols require a license.<sup id="cite_ref-elperiodic.ad_147-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elperiodic.ad-147">[146]</a></sup> The army has not fought for more than 700 years, and its main responsibility is to present the <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Andorra" title="Flag of Andorra">flag of Andorra</a> at official ceremonial functions.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[150]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[151]</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Marc_Forn%C3%A9_Moln%C3%A9" title="Marc Forné Molné">Marc Forné Molné</a>, Andorra's military budget is strictly from voluntary donations, and the availability of full-time volunteers.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[152]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In more recent times there has only been a general emergency call to the popular army of Sometent during the floods of 1982 in the Catalan Pyrenees,<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[153]</a></sup> where 12 citizens perished in Andorra, to help the population and establish a public order along with the Local Police units.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[154]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Police_Corps">Police Corps</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Police Corps">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Andorra_la_Vella_-_Andorra_(3137259845).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Andorra_la_Vella_-_Andorra_%283137259845%29.jpg/220px-Andorra_la_Vella_-_Andorra_%283137259845%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="160" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Andorra_la_Vella_-_Andorra_%283137259845%29.jpg/330px-Andorra_la_Vella_-_Andorra_%283137259845%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/Andorra_la_Vella_-_Andorra_%283137259845%29.jpg/440px-Andorra_la_Vella_-_Andorra_%283137259845%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1932" data-file-height="1403"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Andorra_la_Vella_-_Andorra_(3137259845).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Police_Corps_of_Andorra" title="Police Corps of Andorra">National Police</a> patrolling the central area of the capital city
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Police_Corps_of_Andorra" title="Police Corps of Andorra">Police Corps of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Andorra maintains a small but modern and well-equipped internal police force, with around 240 police officers supported by civilian assistants. The principal services supplied by the corps are uniformed community policing, criminal detection, border control, and traffic policing. There are also small specialist units including police dogs, mountain rescue, and a bomb disposal team.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[155]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="GIPA">GIPA</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: GIPA">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The <i>Grup d'Intervenció Policia d'Andorra</i> (GIPA) is a small special forces unit trained in <a href="/wiki/Counter-terrorism" title="Counter-terrorism">counter-terrorism</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hostage_negotiator" class="mw-redirect" title="Hostage negotiator">hostage recovery</a> tasks. Although it is the closest in style to an active military force, it is part of the <a href="/wiki/Police_Corps_of_Andorra" title="Police Corps of Andorra">Police Corps</a>, and not the <a href="/wiki/Military_of_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="Military of Andorra">army</a>. As terrorist and hostage situations are a rare threat to the country, the GIPA is commonly assigned to prisoner escort duties, and at other times to routine policing.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[156]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fire_brigade">Fire brigade</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Fire brigade">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The Andorran Fire Brigade, with headquarters at <a href="/wiki/Santa_Coloma_d%27Andorra" title="Santa Coloma d'Andorra">Santa Coloma</a>, operates from four modern fire stations, and has a staff of around 120 firefighters. The service is equipped with 16 heavy appliances (fire tenders, turntable ladders, and specialist four-wheel drive vehicles), four light support vehicles (cars and vans) and four ambulances.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[157]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Historically, the families of the six ancient parishes of Andorra maintained local arrangements to assist each other in fighting fires. The first fire pump purchased by the government was acquired in 1943. Serious fires which lasted for two days in December 1959 led to calls for a permanent fire service, and the Andorran Fire Brigade was formed on 21 April 1961.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[158]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The fire service maintains full-time cover with five fire crews on duty at any time: two at the brigade's headquarters in Santa Coloma, and one crew at each of the other three fire stations.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[159]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parishes">Parishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Parishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Andorra" title="Parishes of Andorra">Parishes of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Andorra consists of seven parishes: </p>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_geography">Physical geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Physical geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Due to its location in the eastern <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> mountain range, Andorra consists predominantly of rugged mountains, the highest being the <a href="/wiki/Coma_Pedrosa" title="Coma Pedrosa">Coma Pedrosa</a> at 2,942 metres (9,652&nbsp;ft), and the average elevation of Andorra is 1,996 metres (6,549&nbsp;ft).<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[160]</a></sup> These are dissected by three narrow valleys in a Y shape that combine into one as the main stream, the <a href="/wiki/Gran_Valira" title="Gran Valira">Gran Valira</a> river, leaves the country for Spain (at Andorra's lowest point of 840&nbsp;m or 2,756&nbsp;ft). Andorra's land area is 468&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (181&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi). </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Phytogeography" title="Phytogeography">Phytogeographically</a>, Andorra belongs to the Atlantic European province of the <a href="/wiki/Circumboreal_Region" title="Circumboreal Region">Circumboreal Region</a> within the <a href="/wiki/Boreal_Kingdom" title="Boreal Kingdom">Boreal Kingdom</a>. According to the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Fund_for_Nature" title="World Wide Fund for Nature">WWF</a>, the territory of Andorra belongs to the <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a> of <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees_conifer_and_mixed_forests" title="Pyrenees conifer and mixed forests">Pyrenees conifer and mixed forests</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_162-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-162">[161]</a></sup> Andorra had a 2018 <a href="/wiki/Forest_Landscape_Integrity_Index" title="Forest Landscape Integrity Index">Forest Landscape Integrity Index</a> mean score of 4.45/10, ranking it 127<sup>th</sup> globally out of 172 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-FLII-Supplementary_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FLII-Supplementary-163">[162]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Andorra has <a href="/wiki/Alpine_climate" title="Alpine climate">alpine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental</a> and <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">oceanic climates</a>, depending on altitude. Its higher elevation means there is, on average, more snow in winter and it is slightly cooler in summer. The diversity of landmarks, the different orientation of the valleys and the irregularity relief typical of the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climates</a> make the country have a great diversity of <a href="/wiki/Microclimate" title="Microclimate">microclimates</a> that hinder the general dominance of the <a href="/wiki/Mountain_climate" class="mw-redirect" title="Mountain climate">high mountain climate</a>. The great differences of altitude in the minimum and maximum points, together with the influence of a Mediterranean climate, develop the climate of the Andorran Pyrenees. </p>
      <p>When in precipitation, a global model characterized by convective and abundant rains can be defined during spring and summer, which can last until autumn (May, June and August are usually the rainiest months); In winter, however, it is less rainy, except in the highlands, subject to the influence of fronts from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Europe" title="Atlantic Europe">Atlantic</a>, which explains the great amount of snowfall in the Andorran mountains. The temperature regime is characterized, broadly, by a temperate summer and a long and cold winter; in accordance with the mountainous condition of the Principality.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[163]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed center"> 
       <li class="gallerybox" style="width: 181.33333333333px">
        <div style="width: 181.33333333333px"> 
         <div class="thumb" style="width: 179.33333333333px;">
          <div style="margin:0px auto;">

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Andorra" title="Economy of Andorra">Economy of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="501"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Andorra.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Exports in 2009
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Grandvalira_ski_resort,_Andorra5.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg/220px-Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg/330px-Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg/440px-Grandvalira_ski_resort%2C_Andorra5.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="768"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Grandvalira_ski_resort,_Andorra5.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Scenery of the Andorran mountains at the Grand Valira ski resort, <a href="/wiki/Soldeu" title="Soldeu">Soldeu</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Tourism, the mainstay of Andorra's tiny, well-to-do economy, accounts for roughly 80% of GDP. An estimated 10.2&nbsp;million tourists visit annually,<sup id="cite_ref-es2_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-es2-21">[21]</a></sup> attracted by Andorra's <a href="/wiki/Duty-free_shopping" class="mw-redirect" title="Duty-free shopping">duty-free</a> status and by its summer and winter resorts. </p>
      <p>One of the main sources of income in Andorra is tourism from ski resorts which total over 175&nbsp;km (109&nbsp;mi) of ski ground. The sport brings in over 7 million visitors annually and an estimated 340 million euros per year, sustaining 2,000 direct and 10,000 indirect jobs at present since 2007.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[164]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The banking sector, with its <a href="/wiki/Tax_haven" title="Tax haven">tax haven</a> status, also contributes substantially to the economy with revenues raised exclusively through import tariffs (the financial and insurance sector accounts for approximately 19% of GDP<sup id="cite_ref-fs2013_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fs2013-166">[165]</a></sup>). However, during the <a href="/wiki/European_sovereign-debt_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="European sovereign-debt crisis">European sovereign-debt crisis</a> of the 21st century, the tourist industry suffered a decline, partly caused by a drop in the prices of goods in Spain, undercutting <a href="/wiki/Duty-free_shop" title="Duty-free shop">duty-free shopping</a> and increasing unemployment. On 1 January 2012, a business tax of 10% was introduced,<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[166]</a></sup> followed by a sales tax of 2% a year later, which raised just over 14 million euros in its first quarter.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">[167]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Agricultural production is limited; only 5% of the land is arable, and most food has to be imported. Some tobacco is grown locally. The principal livestock activity is domestic sheep raising. Manufacturing output consists mainly of cigarettes, cigars, and furniture. Andorra's natural resources include hydroelectric power, mineral water, timber, iron ore, and lead.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_3-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Andorra is not a member of the European Union, but enjoys a <a href="/wiki/Andorra%E2%80%93European_Union_relations" title="Andorra–European Union relations">special relationship</a> with it, such as being treated as an EU member for trade in manufactured goods (no tariffs) and as a non-EU member for agricultural products. Andorra lacked a currency of its own and used both the <a href="/wiki/French_franc" title="French franc">French franc</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_peseta" title="Spanish peseta">Spanish peseta</a> in banking transactions until 31 December 1999, when both currencies were replaced by the EU's single currency, the euro. Coins and notes of both the franc and the peseta remained legal tender in Andorra until 31 December 2002. Andorra negotiated to issue its own euro coins, beginning in 2014. </p>
      <p>Andorra has traditionally had one of the world's lowest unemployment rates. In 2019 it stood at 2%.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[168]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>On 31 May 2013, it was announced that Andorra intended to legislate for the introduction of an income tax by the end of June, against a background of increasing dissatisfaction with the existence of tax havens among EU members.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">[169]</a></sup> The announcement was made following a meeting in Paris between the Head of Government <a href="/wiki/Antoni_Mart%C3%AD" title="Antoni Martí">Antoni Martí</a> and the French President and Prince of Andorra <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="François Hollande">François Hollande</a>. Hollande welcomed the move as part of a process of Andorra "bringing its taxation in line with international standards".<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">[170]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>By the mid-2010s, the financial system comprised five banking groups,<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[171]</a></sup> one specialised credit entity, eight investment undertaking management entities, three asset management companies, and 29 insurance companies, 14 of which are branches of foreign insurance companies authorised to operate in the principality.<sup id="cite_ref-fs2013_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fs2013-166">[165]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Els_Cortals_d%27Encamp_-_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Els_Cortals_d%27Encamp_-_1.jpg/220px-Els_Cortals_d%27Encamp_-_1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Els_Cortals_d%27Encamp_-_1.jpg/330px-Els_Cortals_d%27Encamp_-_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/17/Els_Cortals_d%27Encamp_-_1.jpg/440px-Els_Cortals_d%27Encamp_-_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3672" data-file-height="2410"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Els_Cortals_d%27Encamp_-_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>The town of <a href="/wiki/Encamp" title="Encamp">Encamp</a>, as seen from the Vall dels Cortals
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Andorra" title="Demographics of Andorra">Demographics of Andorra</a>
      </div>

      <p>The population of Andorra is estimated at 77,006 (2018).<sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-UN_WPP_2019_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN_WPP_2019-16">[16]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Andorran_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Andorran people">Andorrans</a> are a <a href="/wiki/Romance-speaking_world" title="Romance-speaking world">Romance</a> <a href="/wiki/Ethnic_group" title="Ethnic group">ethnic group</a> of originally <a href="/wiki/Catalans" title="Catalans">Catalan</a> descent.<sup id="cite_ref-Minahan_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Minahan-17">[17]</a></sup> The population has grown from 5,000 in 1900. </p>
      <p>Two-thirds of residents lack Andorran nationality and do not have the right to vote in communal elections. Moreover, they are not allowed to be elected as prime minister<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[173]</a></sup> or to own more than 33% of the capital stock of a privately held company.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[174]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[176]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">[177]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Andorra" title="Languages of Andorra">Languages of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The historic and <a href="/wiki/Official_language" title="Official language">official language</a> is <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Romance_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Romance language">Romance language</a>. The Andorran government encourages the use of Catalan. It funds a Commission for Catalan <a href="/wiki/Toponymy" title="Toponymy">Toponymy</a> in Andorra (Catalan: <i lang="ca" title="Catalan-language text">Comissió de Toponímia d'Andorra</i>), and provides free Catalan classes to assist immigrants. Andorran television and radio stations use Catalan. </p>
      <p>Because of immigration, historical links, and close geographic proximity, Spanish, Portuguese and French are commonly spoken. Most Andorran residents can speak one or more of these, in addition to Catalan. English is less commonly spoken among the general population, though it is understood to varying degrees in the major tourist resorts. Andorra is one of only four European countries (together with France, <a href="/wiki/Monaco" title="Monaco">Monaco</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[178]</a></sup> that have never signed the <a href="/wiki/Framework_Convention_for_the_Protection_of_National_Minorities" title="Framework Convention for the Protection of National Minorities">Council of Europe Framework Convention on National Minorities</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[179]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>According to the <i>Observatori Social d'Andorra</i>, the linguistic usage in Andorra is as follows:<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[180]</a></sup> </p> 
      <table border="0" style="border:1px solid #999; background:#fff;"> 
       <tbody>
        <tr style="text-align:center;"> 
         <th style="background:#ccc;">Mother tongue</th> 
         <th>% </th>
        </tr> 
        <tr style="text-align:center;"> 
         <td style="background:#ccc;"><a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a></td> 
         <td>38.8% </td>
        </tr> 
        <tr style="text-align:center;"> 
         <td style="background:#ccc;"><a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a></td>

      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The population of Andorra is predominantly (88.2%) Catholic.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[181]</a></sup> Their patron saint is <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Meritxell" title="Our Lady of Meritxell">Our Lady of Meritxell</a>. Though it is not an official state religion, the constitution acknowledges a special relationship with the Catholic Church, offering some special privileges to that group.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify"><span title="The text near this tag may need clarification or removal of jargon. (August 2014)">clarification needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Other Christian denominations include the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Anglican Church">Anglican Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Unification_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Unification Church">Unification Church</a>, the <a href="/wiki/New_Apostolic_Church" title="New Apostolic Church">New Apostolic Church</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>. The small <a href="/wiki/Islam_in_Andorra" title="Islam in Andorra">Muslim community</a> is primarily made up of North African immigrants.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[182]</a></sup> There is a small community of <a href="/wiki/Hinduism" title="Hinduism">Hindus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%27%C3%AD_Faith_in_Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="Bahá'í Faith in Andorra">Bahá'ís</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-ARDA05_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARDA05-184">[183]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Wolfram_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wolfram-185">[184]</a></sup> and roughly 100 Jews live in Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[185]</a></sup> (See <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Andorra" title="History of the Jews in Andorra">History of the Jews in Andorra</a>.) </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Largest_cities">Largest cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Largest cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Children between the ages of 6 and 16 are required by law to have full-time education. Education up to secondary level is provided free of charge by the government. </p>
      <p>There are three systems of school, Andorran, French and Spanish, which use Catalan, French and Spanish languages respectively, as the main language of instruction. Parents may choose which system their children attend. All schools are built and maintained by Andorran authorities, but teachers in the French and Spanish schools are paid for the most part by France and Spain. 39% of Andorran children attend Andorran schools, 33% attend French schools, and 28% Spanish schools. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_of_Andorra">University of Andorra</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: University of Andorra">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Universitat_d%27Andorra" title="Universitat d'Andorra">Universitat d'Andorra</a> (UdA) is the state public university and is the only university in Andorra. It was established in 1997. The university provides first-level degrees in nursing, computer science, business administration, and educational sciences, in addition to higher professional education courses. The only two graduate schools in Andorra are the Nursing School and the School of Computer Science, the latter having a PhD programme. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Virtual_Studies_Centre">Virtual Studies Centre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Virtual Studies Centre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The geographical complexity of the country as well as the small number of students prevents the University of Andorra from developing a full academic programme, and it serves principally as a centre for virtual studies, connected to Spanish and French universities. The Virtual Studies Centre (Centre d'Estudis Virtuals) at the University runs approximately 20 different academic degrees at both undergraduate and postgraduate levels in fields including tourism, law, Catalan <a href="/wiki/Philology" title="Philology">philology</a>, humanities, psychology, political sciences, audiovisual communication, telecommunications engineering, and East Asia studies. The centre also runs various postgraduate programmes and continuing-education courses for professionals. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transport">Transport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Transport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Transport_in_Andorra" title="Transport in Andorra">Transport in Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Andorra%E2%80%93La_Seu_d%27Urgell_Airport" title="Andorra–La Seu d'Urgell Airport">Andorra–La Seu d'Urgell Airport</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Pirineus_-_la_Seu_d%27Urgell_airport.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Pirineus_-_la_Seu_d%27Urgell_airport.jpg/220px-Pirineus_-_la_Seu_d%27Urgell_airport.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="171" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Pirineus_-_la_Seu_d%27Urgell_airport.jpg/330px-Pirineus_-_la_Seu_d%27Urgell_airport.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Pirineus_-_la_Seu_d%27Urgell_airport.jpg/440px-Pirineus_-_la_Seu_d%27Urgell_airport.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3244" data-file-height="2518"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Pirineus_-_la_Seu_d%27Urgell_airport.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Andorra%E2%80%93La_Seu_d%27Urgell_Airport" title="Andorra–La Seu d'Urgell Airport">Andorra–La Seu d'Urgell Airport</a>, located 12&nbsp;km away from Andorra, in <a href="/wiki/Montferrer_i_Castellb%C3%B2" title="Montferrer i Castellbò">Montferrer i Castellbò</a> (<a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalonia</a>, Eastern <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Until the 20th century, Andorra had very limited transport links to the outside world, and development of the country was affected by its physical isolation. Even now, the nearest major airports at Toulouse and Barcelona are both three hours' drive from Andorra. </p>
      <p>Andorra has a road network of 279&nbsp;km (173&nbsp;mi), of which 76&nbsp;km (47&nbsp;mi) is unpaved. The two main roads out of <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a> are the CG-1 to the Spanish border near <a href="/wiki/Sant_Juli%C3%A0_de_L%C3%B2ria" title="Sant Julià de Lòria">Sant Julià de Lòria</a>, and the CG-2 to the French border via the Envalira Tunnel near <a href="/wiki/El_Pas_de_la_Casa" title="El Pas de la Casa">El Pas de la Casa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-mobi_187-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mobi-187">[186]</a></sup> Bus services cover all metropolitan areas and many rural communities, with services on most major routes running half-hourly or more frequently during peak travel times. There are frequent long-distance bus services from Andorra to <a href="/wiki/Barcelona" title="Barcelona">Barcelona</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, plus a daily tour from the former city. Bus services mostly are run by private companies, but some local ones are operated by the government. </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:AGC_Z_27500.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AGC_Z_27500.jpg/220px-AGC_Z_27500.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="110" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AGC_Z_27500.jpg/330px-AGC_Z_27500.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/AGC_Z_27500.jpg/440px-AGC_Z_27500.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1500"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:AGC_Z_27500.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A train at <a href="/wiki/Latour-de-Carol" title="Latour-de-Carol">Latour-de-Carol</a> (La Tor de Querol), one of the two stations serving Andorra. Andorra has no railways, although the line connecting Latour-de-Carol and <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a>, which in turn connects to France's <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">TGVs</a> at Toulouse, runs within two kilometres (1.2 miles) of the Andorran border.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>There are no airports for fixed-wing aircraft within Andorra's borders but there are, however, heliports in <a href="/wiki/La_Massana" title="La Massana">La Massana</a> (Camí Heliport), <a href="/wiki/Arinsal" title="Arinsal">Arinsal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Escaldes-Engordany" title="Escaldes-Engordany">Escaldes-Engordany</a> with commercial helicopter services<sup id="cite_ref-heliand_188-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-heliand-188">[187]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-helitrans_189-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-helitrans-189">[188]</a></sup> and an airport located in the neighbouring Spanish comarca of <a href="/wiki/Alt_Urgell" title="Alt Urgell">Alt Urgell</a>, 12 kilometres (7.5 miles) south of the Andorran-Spanish border.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[189]</a></sup> Since July 2015, <a href="/wiki/Andorra%E2%80%93La_Seu_d%27Urgell_Airport" title="Andorra–La Seu d'Urgell Airport">Andorra–La Seu d'Urgell Airport</a> has operated commercial flights to <a href="/wiki/Adolfo_Su%C3%A1rez_Madrid%E2%80%93Barajas_Airport" title="Adolfo Suárez Madrid–Barajas Airport">Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca_Airport" title="Palma de Mallorca Airport">Palma de Mallorca</a>, and is the <a href="/wiki/Airline_hub" title="Airline hub">main hub</a> for <a href="/wiki/Air_Andorra" title="Air Andorra">Air Andorra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Andorra_Airlines" title="Andorra Airlines">Andorra Airlines</a>. As of 11 July 2018, there are no regular commercial flights at the airport. </p>
      <p>Nearby airports located in Spain and France provide access to international flights for the principality. The nearest airports are at <a href="/wiki/Perpignan%E2%80%93Rivesaltes_Airport" title="Perpignan–Rivesaltes Airport">Perpignan</a>, France (156 kilometres or 97 miles from Andorra) and <a href="/wiki/Lleida-Alguaire_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Lleida-Alguaire Airport">Lleida</a>, Spain (160 kilometres or 99 miles from Andorra). The largest nearby airports are at Toulouse, France (165 kilometres or 103 miles from Andorra) and Barcelona, Spain (215 kilometres or 134 miles from Andorra). There are hourly bus services from both Barcelona and Toulouse airports to Andorra. </p>
      <p>The nearest railway station is <a href="/wiki/L%27Hospitalet-pr%C3%A8s-l%27Andorre" title="L'Hospitalet-près-l'Andorre">L'Hospitalet-près-l'Andorre</a> 10&nbsp;km (6&nbsp;mi) east of Andorra which is on the <span class="nowrap">1,435&nbsp;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">4&nbsp;ft&nbsp;<span class="frac">8<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r993651011">.mw-parser-output .sr-only{border:0;clip:rect(0,0,0,0);height:1px;margin:-1px;overflow:hidden;padding:0;position:absolute;width:1px;white-space:nowrap}</style><span class="sr-only">&nbsp;</span><sup>1</sup>⁄<sub>2</sub></span>&nbsp;in</span>)<a href="/wiki/Standard_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Standard gauge">-gauge</a> line from <a href="/wiki/Latour-de-Carol" title="Latour-de-Carol">Latour-de-Carol</a> (25&nbsp;km or 16&nbsp;mi) southeast of Andorra, to <a href="/wiki/Toulouse" title="Toulouse">Toulouse</a> and on to Paris by the French <a href="/wiki/TGV" title="TGV">high-speed trains</a>. This line is operated by the <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a>. Latour-de-Carol has a scenic <span class="nowrap">1,000&nbsp;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">3&nbsp;ft&nbsp;<span class="frac">3
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r993651011"><span class="sr-only">&nbsp;</span><sup>3</sup>⁄<sub>8</sub></span>&nbsp;in</span>) <span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Metre_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Metre gauge">metre gauge</a></span> <a href="/wiki/Yellow_Train" class="mw-redirect" title="Yellow Train">trainline</a> to <a href="/wiki/Villefranche-de-Conflent" title="Villefranche-de-Conflent">Villefranche-de-Conflent</a>, as well as the SNCF's <span class="nowrap">1,435&nbsp;mm</span> gauge line connecting to <a href="/wiki/Perpignan" title="Perpignan">Perpignan</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/RENFE" class="mw-redirect" title="RENFE">RENFE's</a> <span class="nowrap">1,668&nbsp;mm</span> (<span class="nowrap">5&nbsp;ft&nbsp;<span class="frac">5
         <link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r993651011"><span class="sr-only">&nbsp;</span><sup>21</sup>⁄<sub>32</sub></span>&nbsp;in</span>) <a href="/wiki/Iberian_gauge" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberian gauge">-gauge</a> line to Barcelona.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[190]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[191]</a></sup> There are also direct <a href="/wiki/Intercit%C3%A9s#Night_trains" title="Intercités">Intercités de Nuit</a> trains between L'Hospitalet-près-l'Andorre and Paris on certain dates.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[192]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Media_and_telecommunications">Media and telecommunications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Media and telecommunications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Telecommunications_in_Andorra" title="Telecommunications in Andorra">Telecommunications in Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Andorra_Telecom" title="Andorra Telecom">Andorra Telecom</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:RTVA_logotip.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/65/RTVA_logotip.png/220px-RTVA_logotip.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="72" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/65/RTVA_logotip.png 1.5x" data-file-width="271" data-file-height="89"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:RTVA_logotip.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Radio_i_Televisio_d%27Andorra" class="mw-redirect" title="Radio i Televisio d'Andorra">RTVA</a>, the public service television and radio broadcaster in Andorra
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Andorra_Telecom_2019_logo.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Andorra_Telecom_2019_logo.svg/220px-Andorra_Telecom_2019_logo.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="35" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Andorra_Telecom_2019_logo.svg/330px-Andorra_Telecom_2019_logo.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Andorra_Telecom_2019_logo.svg/440px-Andorra_Telecom_2019_logo.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="2501" data-file-height="393"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Andorra_Telecom_2019_logo.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Andorra_Telecom" title="Andorra Telecom">Andorra Telecom</a>, the national telecom company in Andorra
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>In Andorra, mobile and fixed telephone and internet services are operated exclusively by the Andorran national telecommunications company, SOM, also known as <a href="/wiki/Andorra_Telecom" title="Andorra Telecom">Andorra Telecom</a> (STA). The same company also manages the technical infrastructure for national broadcasting of digital television and radio.<sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">[193]</a></sup> In 2010 Andorra became the first country to provide a direct <a href="/wiki/Optical_fiber" title="Optical fiber">optical fiber</a> link to all homes (<a href="/wiki/FTTx" class="mw-redirect" title="FTTx">FTTH</a>) and businesses.<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">[194]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The first commercial radio station to broadcast was <a href="/wiki/Radio_Andorra" title="Radio Andorra">Radio Andorra</a>, which was active from 1939 to 1981.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">[195]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">[196]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">[197]</a></sup> On 12 October 1989, the General Council established radio and television as essential public services creating and managing the entity ORTA, becoming on 13 April 2000, in the public company <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A0dio_i_Televisi%C3%B3_d%27Andorra" title="Ràdio i Televisió d'Andorra">Ràdio i Televisió d'Andorra</a> (RTVA).<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">[198]</a></sup> In 1990, the public radio was founded on the Radio Nacional d'Andorra. As an autochthonous television channel, there is only the national public television network Andorra Televisió, created in 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">[199]</a></sup> Additional TV and radio stations from Spain and France are available via digital terrestrial television and IPTV.<sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">[200]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>There are three national newspapers, <i><a href="/wiki/Diari_d%27Andorra" title="Diari d'Andorra">Diari d'Andorra</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/El_Peri%C3%B2dic_d%27Andorra" title="El Periòdic d'Andorra">El Periòdic d'Andorra</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Bondia_(newspaper)" title="Bondia (newspaper)">Bondia</a></i> as well as several local newspapers.<sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">[201]</a></sup> The history of the Andorran press begins in the period between 1917 and 1937 with the appearance of several periodicals papers such as <i>Les Valls d'Andorra</i> (1917), <i>Nova Andorra</i> (1932) and <i>Andorra Agrícola</i> (1933).<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">[202]</a></sup> In 1974, the <i>Poble Andorrà</i> became the first regular newspaper in Andorra.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">[203]</a></sup> There is also an <a href="/wiki/Amateur_radio" title="Amateur radio">amateur radio</a> society<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">[204]</a></sup> and news agency ANA with independent management.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">[205]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Andorra&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Andorra" title="Culture of Andorra">Culture of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Andorra" title="Music of Andorra">Music of Andorra</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The official and historic language is <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>. Thus the culture is <a href="/wiki/Catalonia" title="Catalonia">Catalan</a>, with its own specificity. </p>
      <p>Andorra is home to folk dances like the contrapàs and marratxa, which survive in <a href="/wiki/Sant_Juli%C3%A0_de_L%C3%B2ria" title="Sant Julià de Lòria">Sant Julià de Lòria</a> especially. Andorran folk music has similarities to the music of its neighbours, but is especially <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Catalonia" title="Music of Catalonia">Catalan</a> in character, especially in the presence of dances such as the <a href="/wiki/Sardana" title="Sardana">sardana</a>. Other Andorran folk dances include contrapàs in <a href="/wiki/Andorra_la_Vella" title="Andorra la Vella">Andorra la Vella</a> and Saint Anne's dance in Escaldes-Engordany. Andorra's national holiday is <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Meritxell" title="Our Lady of Meritxell">Our Lady of Meritxell</a> Day, 8 September.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_3-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-3">[3]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Among the more important festivals and traditions are the <a href="/wiki/Can%C3%B2lic" title="Canòlic">Canólich Gathering</a> in May, the Roser d'Ordino in July, the Meritxell Day (National Day of Andorra), the Andorra la Vella Fair, the <a href="/wiki/Sant_Jordi" class="mw-redirect" title="Sant Jordi">Sant Jordi Day</a>, the Santa Llúcia Fair, the Festivity from La Candelera to Canillo, the <a href="/wiki/Carnival" title="Carnival">Carnival</a> of Encamp, the sung of caramelles, the Festivity of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Stephen" title="Saint Stephen">Sant Esteve</a> and the Festa del Poble.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">[206]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">[207]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Andorra participated regularly in the <a href="/wiki/Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="Eurovision Song Contest">Eurovision Song Contest</a> between 2004 and 2009, being the only <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_in_the_Eurovision_Song_Contest" title="List of countries in the Eurovision Song Contest">participating country</a> presenting songs in <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">Catalan</a>. </p>
      <p>In popular folklore, the best-known Andorran legends are the legend of Charlemagne, according to which this Frankish King would have founded the country, the White Lady of <a href="/wiki/Auviny%C3%A0" class="mw-redirect" title="Auvinyà">Auvinyà</a>, the <a href="/wiki/El_buner_d%27Ordino" title="El buner d'Ordino">Buner d'Ordino</a>, the legend of <a href="/wiki/Engolasters" title="Engolasters">Engolasters Lake</a> and the legend of <a href="/wiki/Our_Lady_of_Meritxell" title="Our Lady of Meritxell">Our Lady of Meritxell</a>. </p>
      <p>Andorran gastronomy is mainly <a href="/wiki/Catalan_cuisine" title="Catalan cuisine">Catalan</a>, although it has also adopted other elements of <a href="/wiki/French_cuisine" title="French cuisine">French</a> and <a href="/wiki/Italian_cuisine" title="Italian cuisine">Italian</a> cuisines. The cuisine of the country has similar characteristics with the neighbors of the <a href="/wiki/Cerdanya" title="Cerdanya">Cerdanya</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Alt_Urgell" title="Alt Urgell">Alt Urgell</a>, with whom it has a strong cultural ties. Andorra's cuisine is marked by its nature as mountain valleys. Typical dishes of the country are the <a href="/wiki/Quince" title="Quince">quince</a> <a href="/wiki/Aioli" title="Aioli">all-i-oli</a>, the duck with winter pear, the lamb in the oven with nuts, pork civet, the massegada cake, the escarole with pear trees, confited duck and mushrooms, <a href="/wiki/Escudella" class="mw-redirect" title="Escudella">escudella</a>, spinach with raisins and pine nuts, jelly marmalade, stuffed murgues (mushrooms) with pork, <a href="/wiki/Dandelion" class="mw-redirect" title="Dandelion">dandelion</a> salad and the Andorran <a href="/wiki/Trout" title="Trout">trout of river</a>. To drink, the <a href="/wiki/Mulled_wine" title="Mulled wine">mulled wine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Beer" title="Beer">beer</a> are also popular.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">[208]</a></sup> Some of the dishes are very common in the <a href="/wiki/Alt_Pirineu_i_Aran" title="Alt Pirineu i Aran">mountainous regions of Catalonia</a>, such as <a href="/wiki/Trinxat" title="Trinxat">trinxat</a>, <a href="/wiki/Embutido" title="Embutido">embotits</a>, cooked snails, rice with mushrooms, mountain rice and <a href="/wiki/Mat%C3%B3" title="Mató">mató</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">[209]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Pre-Romanesque" class="mw-redirect" title="Pre-Romanesque">Pre-Romanesque</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_art" title="Romanesque art">Romanesque art</a> are one of the most important artistic manifestations and characteristics of the Principality. The Romanesque one allows to know the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Parishes_of_Andorra" title="Parishes of Andorra">parochial communities</a>, the relations of (social and political) power and the national culture. There are a total of forty Romanesque churches that stand out as being small austere ornamentation constructions, as well as <a href="/wiki/Romanesque_architecture" title="Romanesque architecture">bridges</a>, fortresses and <a href="/wiki/Manor_houses" class="mw-redirect" title="Manor houses">manor houses</a> of the same period.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">[210]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">[211]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/w/index.php?title=Summer_solstice_fire_festivals&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Summer solstice fire festivals (page does not exist)">Summer solstice fire festivals</a> in the Pyrenees was included as <a href="/wiki/Intangible_cultural_heritage" title="Intangible cultural heritage">UNESCO Intangible cultural heritage</a> in 2015.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">[212]</a></sup> Also the <a href="/wiki/Madriu-Perafita-Claror_Valley" title="Madriu-Perafita-Claror Valley">Madriu-Perafita-Claror Valley</a> became Andorra's first, and to date its only, <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Site</a> in 2004, with a small extension in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">[213]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-215" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-215">[214]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed center">
